## Archived 2026-05-15 (RESTORE-UX-FEEDBACK-01)

### RESTORE-UX-FEEDBACK-01 — optimistic restore + use returned entity

Filed 2026-05-14 by UX-Full-Audit 2026-05-14/15 (Bug A reframe).
P3 IMPROVEMENT. Closed 2026-05-15 in commit `7d68126`.

Context: the 2026-05-14 Articles-Trash Restore user report was
**not a code bug** (workbox "No route found" message was misread
as blocking; the actual restore POST fired correctly). The real
signal was the `[Violation] 'click' handler took 419ms` console
line — perception-lag from chained roundtrips inside a single
synchronous handler. Combined with the "stay in trash view"
pattern post-restore, the feedback was subtle enough that users
reported "doesn't work" even though the backend state was
correct. The audit's "User-perceived bug ≠ code bug: the
perception-lag class" lessons-learned entry captures the
diagnostic pattern.

What landed:

- **`ArticleList.handleRestore` + `Dashboard.handleRestore`
  refactor**: optimistic update — drop the trash row BEFORE
  awaiting the network roundtrip. Use the entity returned by
  POST `/restore` to prepend to the live list. Skip the full
  `/api/articles` or `/api/books` refetch that produced the bulk
  of the lag.
- **Revert on error**: re-add the row to trash state in the catch
  branch so a failed restore doesn't vanish the row entirely.
  Pre-existing silent-failure bug in `ArticleList` (non-ApiError
  exceptions were swallowed) is also closed by the new catch.
- **`Dashboard.handleRestore` signature**: changed from `(id)` to
  `(book)` so the revert path has the entity to push back. Both
  callsites (`TrashCard` + list-view button) updated.
- **i18n**: added `ui.dashboard.restored` +
  `ui.dashboard.restore_failed` across all 8 catalogs (DE, EN,
  ES, FR, EL, PT, TR, JA). Dashboard previously had no success
  toast at all — silent success was itself a UX bug. Added
  English + DE + per-language proper-character translations
  following the catalog's existing transliteration policy.
- **E2E coverage**: new `e2e/smoke/trash-restore-optimistic.spec.ts`
  (4 tests) pins the optimistic-update + revert-on-error
  behavior across both surfaces:
  - "trash row disappears before the restore request resolves"
    (×2, articles + books) — delays the restore via
    `page.route()` and asserts the row is hidden within 500ms.
    Regression-pin: if the handler reverts to "await restore +
    refetch", the row stays visible until the route resolves
    and the test fails.
  - "trash row is reverted when the restore request fails"
    (×2, articles + books) — fulfills the route with 500 and
    asserts the trash row reappears.

Both surfaces mirrored per the Articles-vs-Books parity rule
from lessons-learned. Full suite green: backend 1698 passed (1
skipped), frontend 1000 passed.

Cross-references:

- Pairs with the closed PLUGIN-SETTINGS-TESTID-COVERAGE-01 and
  NOTIFY-ERROR-APIERROR-COVERAGE-01 as the four P2/P3 items
  filed by UX-Full-Audit 2026-05-14/15. All four are now
  closed.

---

## Archived 2026-05-15 (THEME-TOKEN-COMPLETENESS-AUDIT-01)

### THEME-TOKEN-COMPLETENESS-AUDIT-01 — close 5 theme-token gaps

Filed 2026-05-15 by UX-Full-Audit 2026-05-15 (G4-F4) as a
RECURRING-ISSUE-CLASS (same bug class fired in v0.31.0 Pre-
Release Audit). P3 IMPROVEMENT. Closed same day in commit
`cacb7e5`.

What landed:

- **Cleanup pass**: 15 unique tokens cross-checked across 134
  `var(--token, #hex-fallback)` callsites. 5 tokens had gaps
  spanning 12 callsites:
  - `--error` → replaced with `--danger` (6 callsites, 5 files).
    Pruned the duplicate token rather than aliasing, since
    `--danger` already had a definition in every palette × mode.
    Files: `AiSetupWizard.tsx`, `ArticleImageUpload.tsx`,
    `articles/PublicationsPanel.tsx`, `pages/ArticleEditor.tsx`
    (2 sites), `pages/ArticleEditor.module.css`.
  - `--success-light`, `--warning-light`, `--warning-dark`,
    `--bg-warning` → defined in `:root` (light) +
    `[data-theme="dark"]` (dark) blocks of
    `frontend/src/styles/global.css`. Cascade through `:root`
    serves every current callsite without per-palette tuning;
    palette overrides land in the per-palette blocks if they
    ever differ.
- **Drift prevention**: `scripts/audit_theme_tokens.py`
  classifies every callsite by palette × mode coverage.
  `--enforce` exits 1 on any gap; `--quiet` skips the full
  per-token coverage table. Pre-commit hook
  `theme-token-completeness` runs `--enforce --quiet` on every
  commit touching `frontend/src/**/*.{ts,tsx,css}`. Verified
  Passed on the full repo.

Post-cleanup: all 15 tokens covered in every palette × mode.
Full suite green: backend 1698 passed (1 skipped), frontend
1000 passed.

Reconciliation with the audit's "111 callsites" figure: the
script at archive time counted 134. Drift between audit date
and archival date — same order of magnitude, audit pattern
reproducible.

Future drift prevention encoded in the pre-commit hook, not in
release-cycle audit ritual. The bug class moves from "recurring"
to "gated by tooling" — every future `var(--token, #fallback)`
callsite that lacks a `--token` definition fails the commit with
a per-file list. No ESLint rule needed (the audit suggested one
as an alternative); the Python classifier is simpler and ships
with diagnostic output.

Lessons-learned entry "Periodic theme-token completeness audit
as pre-release hygiene" supersedes the manual recipe with the
script invocation. The pre-commit hook now does the work the
human ritual used to do.

---

## Archived 2026-05-15 (NOTIFY-ERROR-APIERROR-COVERAGE-01)

### NOTIFY-ERROR-APIERROR-COVERAGE-01 — pass caught errors to notify.error

Filed 2026-05-15 by UX-Full-Audit 2026-05-15 (G4-F1) as
P2-elevated IMPROVEMENT. Closed same day in commit `5ab5619`.

What landed:

- **Cleanup pass: 26 callsites across 9 files** changed to
  pass the caught error as the 2nd arg to `notify.error`.
  - 13 B_FIXABLE (plain message inside `catch (err)`):
    `BackupCompareDialog.tsx` (1), `BookMetadataEditor.tsx` (1),
    `CommentsAdminSection.tsx` (2), `Editor.tsx` (4: spellcheck,
    preview, AI x2), `GitBackupDialog.tsx` (2: `auth_failed`),
    `pages/ArticleList.tsx` (1), `pages/BookEditor.tsx` (1),
    `pages/Dashboard.tsx` (1).
  - 13 A_HAS_VAR (`notify.error(describeError(err))` shape):
    `GitBackupDialog.tsx` (10), `SshKeySection.tsx` (3).
- **`scripts/audit_notify_error_calls.py`**: classifier with
  `--enforce` mode. Buckets every callsite into A_OK /
  C_VALIDATION / B_FIXABLE / A_HAS_VAR using a brace-counting
  catch-scope walker (stdlib-only; regex for catch detection,
  brace balance for scope, string literals skipped so `"}"`
  inside a string does not break the count).
- **Pre-commit hook `notify-error-apierror-coverage`** in
  `.pre-commit-config.yaml`: runs the script with
  `--enforce --quiet` on every commit touching
  `frontend/src/**/*.{ts,tsx}`. Verified Passed on the full
  repo.

Post-cleanup audit numbers: `{'A_OK': 116, 'C_VALIDATION': 22}`.
Zero B_FIXABLE, zero A_HAS_VAR remaining.

Reconciliation with the audit's "99 of 159 bypass" estimate:
the analyzer at archive time found 138 production callsites
(.test files excluded) with 26 fixable. The audit's count
was an overestimate — likely because it counted total
`notify.error` without separating validation-message
callsites (which correctly never had an error to pass) from
in-catch callsites. The actionable gap was smaller than the
audit suggested but the cleanup pattern was real and useful.

Full suite green after the cleanup: backend 1698 passed (1
skipped), frontend 1000 passed.

Future drift prevention: the pre-commit hook is the gate.
Any future reintroduction of a missing-2nd-arg pattern in
production code fails the commit with a per-file list of
fixable sites. No ESLint rule needed (the audit suggested
one as an alternative); the Python classifier is simpler
to maintain and ships with diagnostic output.

---

Filed 2026-05-14 by the first complete mutmut run.
Unblocked the same day when
``MUTMUT-HANDLERS-OFFICE-WBT-COVERAGE-01`` closed. Run +
triaged in the evening of the same day.

What landed:

- ``backend/pyproject.toml`` ``[tool.mutmut]`` — expanded
  ``paths_to_mutate`` to
  ``["app/import_plugins/", "app/services/"]``. Added 20
  services-related test files to ``tests_dir`` plus the
  new ``test_platform_schema.py``.
- ``backend/tests/test_platform_schema.py`` — 21 new unit
  tests for the AR-02 Phase 2 platform-schema validator
  (``load_platform_schemas``, ``get_platform_schema``,
  ``validate_platform_metadata`` with required-field /
  empty-string / empty-list / empty-dict / None / max_tags
  / max_chars edge cases). Closes the 54-mutant no-tests
  pool on this module — the only service file with ZERO

  "Services expansion" section with full per-file
  triage table (20 service files, 7062 mutants), peak
  RSS recorded (~500 MB), 3 sub-followups filed.

Numbers from the fresh evening run after the expansion:

- **Combined: 7526 / 9832 killed = 76.5%**
  (peak RSS ~500 MB on 30 GB dev machine — no OOM)
- ``app/import_plugins/``: 78.7% (unchanged from morning)
- ``app/services/``: 75.7% (new baseline)
- Wall time: ~9 minutes (18.56 mutations/sec)

Both surfaces exceed the >= 60% acceptance criterion.

Sub-followups filed for the high-volume services pools
(filed in backlog P5):

- ``BACKUP-PROJECT-IMPORT-MUTMUT-01`` (34 no-tests in
  per-asset / per-chapter helpers)
- ``BACKUP-SERIALIZER-MUTMUT-01`` (162 + 10 cosmetic-heavy
  pool on output-key string literals)
- ``GIT-BACKUP-MUTMUT-01`` (330 + 57; largest single-file
  pool, mixed cosmetic + real)

These are P5 raise-the-floor investments, not blockers.

The OOM concern from the audit doc's original wording was
based on attempts to mutate the FULL ``app/`` surface (not
just services/). The narrower
``app/import_plugins/ + app/services/`` scope is comfortably
within the dev machine's RAM budget. The next expansion
candidate (``app/routers/`` or ``app/models/``) would still
need its own deliberate audit.

## Archived 2026-05-14 (MUTMUT-HANDLERS-OFFICE-WBT-COVERAGE-01)

### MUTMUT-HANDLERS-OFFICE-WBT-COVERAGE-01 — triage office + wbt survivor pools

Filed 2026-05-14 by the first complete mutmut run.
Triaged + partially closed in the same day via a fresh
mutmut run after ``MUTMUT-OVERRIDES-COERCION-COVERAGE-01``
had already shifted the score from 77.8% to 78.7%
(2179/2770 killed).

Triage outcome (full per-function table in
``docs/audits/mutmut-2026-05-02-import.md``):

**handlers.office** (167 survived + 26 no-tests + 2 timeout):

- ``_OfficeHandlerBaseǁexecute`` (50): mixed — case-flipped
  default-arg literals are cosmetic, None-injections survive
  because tests don't assert on every DB field. Real gap was
  the ``_hard_delete_book`` overwrite path.
- ``_OfficeHandlerBaseǁdetect`` (32): mostly cosmetic;
  warning-string mutations survive against substring-match
  assertions.
- ``_guess_mime`` (31): pure dispatch on mime-suffix table;
  every literal gets XX-wrapped and case-flipped. Killing
  all 31 would mean asserting exact equality with every
  casing variant — test bloat for zero functional payoff.
  Accept.
- ``_convert_to_markdown`` (29): Pandoc cmd-list strings;
  defensive — tests mock subprocess.run entirely so cmd-list
  mutations are invisible.
- ``_is_zip_epub`` (14, no-tests): **DEAD CODE**.
  Documented "Not called from the hot path"; zero production
  callers verified by grep. Function deleted from
  ``backend/app/import_plugins/handlers/office.py``; the
  14-mutant pool disappears on the next mutmut run.
- ``_hard_delete_book`` (12, no-tests): **REAL GAP**. New
  test ``test_execute_overwrite_removes_existing_chapters_and_assets``
  in ``test_office_handlers.py`` exercises the
  ``duplicate_action="overwrite"`` path on the docx handler
  and asserts both chapter AND asset rows for the original
  Book are gone post-overwrite.
- ``_detected_assets`` / ``_import_media`` / ``_split_into_chapters``
  (10 + 7 + 5): small mixed buckets; accept.
- ``_sha256_of_file`` (3 + 2 timeout): expected finding;
  mutmut's range mutation on the chunked-read loop blows out
  the timeout while producing the same hash.

**handlers.wbt** (166 survived + 12 no-tests + 2 timeout):

- ``_guess_mime`` (43): same shape as office; accept.
- ``_purpose_from_path`` (36): pure dispatch on folder-name
  match sets; every literal gets XX-wrapped and case-flipped.
  Accept.
- ``_try_multi_branch_import`` (33): mostly log-message
  mutations + None-args on logger calls. ``logger.warning(None)``
  doesn't crash — it just logs ``"None"`` — so the mutations
  are invisible to tests. Behavioural paths already covered
  by ``test_wbt_multi_branch_import.py``. Accept.
- ``_strip_remote_from_translation_group`` (23): mixed;
  ``continue → break`` and DB-filter ``==``/``!=`` swaps are
  REAL gaps but the function is best-effort cleanup, not
  critical correctness. Accept; small-bucket gap, would
  benefit from a multi-book sibling-loop test if real bugs
  surface.
- ``_extracted_root`` (22): equivalent/cosmetic;
  ``[:16] vs [:17]`` produces a different but still-unique
  SHA-256 prefix (both are unique across all real digests).
- ``_hard_delete_book`` (12, no-tests): **REAL GAP**. New
  test ``test_execute_overwrite_removes_existing_chapters_and_assets``
  in ``test_wbt_handler.py`` mirrors the office handler's
  overwrite test.
- ``_apply_primary_cover`` (6): partially closed by
  tightening ``test_primary_cover_override_rejects_unknown_filename``
  in ``test_wbt_multi_cover.py`` from ``pytest.raises(Exception)``
  to ``pytest.raises(KeyError, match=r"primary_cover=.*nonexistent\.png")``.
  Kills the ``KeyError(None)``, ``available = None``, and
  f-string template case-flip mutations. The remaining
  DB-filter mutations would require a multi-book test
  (small bucket; deferred).
- ``_sha256_of_file`` (2 + 2 timeout): expected finding.
- ``_logger`` (1): equivalent.

**Equivalent-mutation note on the 7 remaining ``overrides``
survivors** (mutmut_12, 14, 16, 22, 24, 26, 28): inspection
confirmed these are behavior-preserving thanks to the broad
``except Exception`` clause and ``bool(None) == bool(False)``
semantics. Cannot be killed without rewriting the function
to either remove the broad except (introduce real failure
modes) or distinguish ``None`` from ``False`` semantically
(gratuitous complexity for no user-visible change).
Documented as equivalent in the audit doc.

What landed:

- ``backend/app/import_plugins/handlers/office.py`` — deleted
  ``_is_zip_epub`` + the unused ``zipfile`` import.
- ``backend/tests/test_office_handlers.py`` — new test
  ``test_execute_overwrite_removes_existing_chapters_and_assets``
  pinning the docx handler's ``_hard_delete_book`` overwrite
  path (12 no-tests mutants).
- ``backend/tests/test_wbt_handler.py`` — new test of the same
  name for the wbt handler (12 no-tests mutants).
- ``backend/tests/test_wbt_multi_cover.py`` — tightened
  ``test_primary_cover_override_rejects_unknown_filename`` to
  pin KeyError type + message substring (3-4
  ``_apply_primary_cover`` mutants).
- ``docs/audits/mutmut-2026-05-02-import.md`` — full triage
  table appended, per-function verdicts documented,
  acceptance-criteria block updated, equivalent-mutation
  note for the 7 ``overrides`` survivors.

Verification: 35/35 tests pass in the touched files in
0.87 s. Full backend suite (`make test` proxy:
`pytest tests/ -q -x --ignore=tests/test_audiobook_export_async.py`)
green at 1660 passed / 1 skipped / 47 warnings / 142.19 s.
``ruff check`` clean. Mutation-score gain confirmation
deferred to the next mutmut run (CI nightly or manual
``poetry run mutmut run``); the expected score is in the
80%+ range after the 38-mutant + 14-dead-code reduction
lands.

Follow-up filed (already open): ``MUTMUT-EXPAND-SCOPE-01``
is now unblocked — its trigger was completion of the
``app/import_plugins/`` triage.

## Archived 2026-05-14 (MUTMUT-OVERRIDES-COERCION-COVERAGE-01)

### MUTMUT-OVERRIDES-COERCION-COVERAGE-01 — kill the overrides.py bool-coercion survivor pool

Filed 2026-05-14 by the first complete mutmut run after
`MUTMUT-STATS-COLLECTION-BUG-01` unblocked stats
collection. The 2026-05-14 audit table flagged ~30
survivors mutmut_5..34 in
`app/import_plugins/overrides.py`, almost all in
`_allow_books_without_author_from_yaml` — the function
reads a single bool flag with permissive coercion and the
existing tests pinned only the strict `True` / `False`
paths.

What landed:

- `backend/tests/test_overrides_yaml_loader.py` — 13
  targeted unit tests, one per branch of the function.
  Uses a `fake_backend` fixture that builds a tmp
  `backend/app/import_plugins/overrides.py` +
  `backend/config/app.yaml` tree and monkeypatches
  `overrides.__file__` so the function's
  `Path(__file__).resolve().parent.parent.parent` resolver
  lands inside the tmp tree. Branches covered:
  missing config file, empty YAML, missing `app` section,
  missing flag key, value `true`, value `false`, value
  `null`, truthy string (`"yes"`), empty string, nonzero
  int (`1`), zero, malformed YAML triggering the
  exception path, and unreadable path (config is a
  directory).
- `backend/pyproject.toml` — registered the new test file
  in `[tool.mutmut] tests_dir` so the next mutation pass
  exercises it against the survivors.
- `docs/audits/mutmut-2026-05-02-import.md` — updated the
  per-module triage table + closed the follow-up entry
  with a pointer to the new test file.

Verification: 13 tests pass in 0.18 s
(`poetry run pytest tests/test_overrides_yaml_loader.py`),
`ruff check` + `ruff format --check` clean. Mutation-pass
verification deferred to the next mutmut run on CI; the
test additions are pure mutation-coverage so the previous
audit's 2156/2770 (77.8%) score should rise without
producing new survivors.

## Archived 2026-05-14 (MUTMUT-STATS-COLLECTION-BUG-01)

### MUTMUT-STATS-COLLECTION-BUG-01 — unblock mutmut stats collection

Filed 2026-05-12 by the test-infrastructure audit when the
existing nightly workflow `.github/workflows/mutation-import.yml`
was triggered via `workflow_dispatch` for the first time and
crashed with `BadTestExecutionCommandsException` during
mutmut's stats-collection phase. Investigation across two
sessions (2026-05-13 partial, 2026-05-14 complete)
identified 5 separate root causes and fixed all 5. First
ever full mutmut run on Bibliogon completed 2026-05-14:
**2156 / 2770 mutants killed = 77.8% mutation score** for
`app/import_plugins/`, exceeding the audit's >= 60% bar.

What landed:

1. **`app/backup_history.py`**: `from __future__ import
   annotations` to defer type-annotation evaluation. mutmut
   places its `def list(self, ...)` trampoline ABOVE the
   `xǁ...__mutmut_orig` original in class bodies; the
   original's `-> list[dict[str, Any]]` annotation then
   resolves `list` against the just-bound class-scope
   trampoline (a function) instead of the builtin and
   crashes with `TypeError: 'function' object is not
   subscriptable`.

2. **`backend/tests/conftest.py`**: seed `config/` +
   `migrations/` into the `mutants/` tree (mutmut only
   copies `app/`, `tests/`, `pyproject.toml`). Without
   `app.yaml.example`, PluginManager defaults
   `entry_point_group` to `pluginforge.plugins` and
   mismatches `HookspecMarker("bibliogon.plugins")`.
   Without `migrations/`, Alembic's env.py crashes with
   `CommandError: Path doesn't exist`.

3. **Robust REPO_ROOT in 4 tests** (`test_docs_parity`,
   `test_plugin_lock_drift_hook`,
   `test_medium_import_roundtrip`,
   `test_medium_import_endpoint`): replaced the fixed-depth
   `Path(__file__).resolve().parent.parent.parent` shortcut
   with directory-predicate walkers that find the actual
   repo root regardless of whether the test lives in
   `backend/tests/` or `mutants/tests/`. Predicates must be
   specific enough — a naive `(p / "plugins").is_dir()`
   matches `backend/plugins/installed/` (left over from
   plugin-install tests) and breaks `make test`.

4. **`test_subscribe_cleanup_removes_subscriber`**: poll on
   `job._subscribers` until empty with a 500 ms deadline so
   the inner async generator's `finally` clause scheduled
   through the event loop gets a chance to run before the
   assertion. mutmut's trampoline wraps every async
   generator in an outer iterator; when `aclose()` runs on
   the outer, the inner's cleanup is async and may not have
   completed when the immediately-following sync assertion
   fires.

5. **Recursion-limit bump + scope narrow + sibling symlink**
   in `tests/conftest.py`: under `MUTANT_UNDER_TEST` raise
   the recursion limit from 5000 to 15000 (mutmut's
   trampoline wrapping adds ~10-15 frames per call;
   FastAPI lifespan stacks overflow at 5000); narrow
   `paths_to_mutate` to `app/import_plugins/` and
   `tests_dir` to the 17 tests that exercise it (full
   `app/` OOM-killed the dev machine on 2026-05-14); when
   the narrow scope copies only `app/import_plugins/`,
   symlink every other `app/*` entry from the real
   `backend/app/` so tests still import `app.database`,
   `app.main`, etc.

Files modified:

- `backend/app/backup_history.py` — future-annotations import.
- `backend/tests/conftest.py` — seed config + migrations,
  symlink docs/plugins/app-siblings, raise recursion limit
  under `MUTANT_UNDER_TEST`.
- `backend/tests/test_docs_parity.py` — REPO_ROOT walker.
- `backend/tests/test_plugin_lock_drift_hook.py` — walker.
- `backend/tests/test_medium_import_roundtrip.py` — walker.
- `backend/tests/test_medium_import_endpoint.py` — walker.
- `backend/tests/test_job_store.py` — timing-robust poll.
- `backend/pyproject.toml` — narrowed `paths_to_mutate` +
  explicit `tests_dir` list.

Verification:

```bash
cd backend
rm -rf mutants && poetry run mutmut run
# ⠼ 2770/2770  🎉 2156 🫥 64  ⏰ 6  🤔 0  🙁 544  🔇 0  🧙 0
# 37.21 mutations/second; exit 0
poetry run pytest --no-header -q | tail -3
# 1648 passed, 1 skipped — make test stays green
```

Detailed per-module triage table + 3 follow-up tasks live
in `docs/audits/mutmut-2026-05-02-import.md`. Of the 614
non-killed entries (544 survived + 64 no-tests + 6
timeout), the bulk live in handler formatter code rather
than in validation paths; the security-sensitive
`_sanitise_rel_path` / `_check_duplicate` helpers were all
killed.

Follow-ups filed in backlog:
- `MUTMUT-OVERRIDES-COERCION-COVERAGE-01` (P5).
- `MUTMUT-HANDLERS-OFFICE-WBT-COVERAGE-01` (P5).
- `MUTMUT-EXPAND-SCOPE-01` (P5).

## Archived 2026-05-13 (PROD-WRITES-ARCHITECTURE-01)

### PROD-WRITES-ARCHITECTURE-01 — route runtime writes through user-overlay

Filed 2026-05-13 by the v0.31.0 Phase 2 release session. Closed
2026-05-13 in the post-handover follow-up session. Trigger was
"dev-docker write failures persist beyond Phase 2 + new
contributors stumble on it" — closed proactively as a clean
refactor since the architecture was already defined via
`_load_app_config`'s existing project + secrets-override merge.

What landed (this commit):

1. New `backend/app/config_overlay.py` module: project / user-
   overlay deep-merge helpers, ruamel round-trip "load-for-edit"
   path that preserves `# INTERNAL` comments, write helpers that
   target `get_data_dir() / "config"` only.
2. `backend/app/routers/settings.py`: all 10+ writes to
   `_base_dir / "config" / "app.yaml"` and `.../plugins/*.yaml`
   route through `config_overlay`. The Settings PATCH /
   pen-name POST / plugin enable / disable / create / delete /
   plugin-config PATCH endpoints now write to the overlay layer
   only.
3. `backend/app/routers/plugin_install.py`: ZIP install copies
   `plugin.yaml` to the user-overlay; `_enable_plugin_in_config`
   and the uninstall path mutate the user-overlay app.yaml.
4. `backend/app/main.py`: `_load_app_config()` now performs a
   four-layer merge (project → user-overlay → secrets-override
   → env-vars); a new `_sync_manager_with_overlay()` helper
   patches `PluginManager._app_config` with the merged view at
   startup so plugin discovery sees the user's enable / disable
   toggles without a restart. Same hook fires after every
   Settings / plugin-install write through
   `_refresh_manager_app_config()` helpers.
5. New `backend/tests/test_config_overlay.py`: 22 tests pinning
   merge semantics, the "writes never touch the project tree"
   invariant, comment-preserving round-trip path, deletion +
   list-merge semantics. The path-isolation invariant test
   matches the headline backlog promise.
6. Existing test fixtures updated (`test_settings_api`,
   `test_plugin_install`, `test_ai_config_refresh`,
   `test_config_loader`): collapse the two overlay layers onto
   the per-test `temp_base` via
   `config_overlay.set_project_config_dir` +
   `monkeypatch.setenv("BIBLIOGON_DATA_DIR", ...)` so existing
   single-file seeds remain the source of truth and assertions
   keep their semantics. `test_config_loader`'s `project_yaml`
   fixture now isolates BIBLIOGON_DATA_DIR so the overlay-layer
   contents from earlier tests in the session do not leak in.

Production Docker stays unchanged because its
`USER bibliogon` + `chown -R bibliogon:bibliogon /app`
makes `/app/config/` writable; the refactor just routes
writes to a different path the prod container also owns
(`/app/data/config/`). Dev-docker (bind-mount UID
mismatch) now succeeds on Settings UI changes + plugin
install / uninstall because writes go to the platformdirs
data dir, which is in the user's `~/.local/share/bibliogon/`
on Linux.

Verification:
- `make test`: 1648 backend + 929 Vitest green (was 1626
  backend pre-refactor; the +22 are the new
  `test_config_overlay.py` cases).
- `poetry run ruff check app/` + `poetry run mypy app/`:
  clean (99 files).
- `poetry run pre-commit run --all-files`: clean.

Reads still merge project + user-overlay (user wins, dicts
deep-merge, lists replace). This means a user who upgraded
from v0.31.x to v0.32.x keeps seeing their existing
`backend/config/app.yaml` content (it's still the bottom
layer); the next Settings write lands in the new
user-overlay layer on top. No data migration needed.

## Archived 2026-05-13 (CRYPTOGRAPHY-V48-MIGRATION-01)

### CRYPTOGRAPHY-V48-MIGRATION-01 — bump cryptography 46.0.7 -> 48.0.0 + pip-audit pass

Filed 2026-05-12 by the dep-update audit. Closed proactively on
2026-05-13 after BACKEND-UPLOAD-SIZE-LIMIT-01. Trigger was
"any CVE in 46.x, OR pair with `pip audit` security review
session (the audit itself yields independent value)" — running
the audit produced independent findings (pillow CVE batch in
launcher; see separate commit `60eb147`).

What landed (2 commits):

1. `3e38cf7` — `cryptography ^46.0.7 -> ^48.0.0` in
   `backend/pyproject.toml` and
   `plugins/bibliogon-plugin-audiobook/pyproject.toml`. Lockfiles
   regenerated via `poetry lock` + `make lock-all-plugins`.
   Stale `bibliogon-plugin-export = 0.30.0` reference in
   `plugins/bibliogon-plugin-git-sync/poetry.lock` cleaned up
   as a side effect of the re-lock pass.
2. `60eb147` — `pillow ^11.2.1 -> ^12.2.0` in
   `launcher/pyproject.toml`. Clears 5 CVEs (CVE-2026-25990,
   CVE-2026-40192, CVE-2026-42308 through 42311). Pillow is a
   launcher-DEV-only dep; the PyInstaller-built launcher
   binary doesn't bundle it. Backend already ran 12.2.0 via
   the manuscripta dep chain.

Compatibility surface (cryptography):

- `backend/app/credential_store.py`: `cryptography.fernet.Fernet`
  — symmetric encryption for stored credentials. Core API,
  stable across versions.
- `backend/app/services/ssh_keys.py`:
  `cryptography.hazmat.primitives.serialization` +
  `Ed25519PrivateKey`. Modern asymmetric primitives, stable.
- `backend/app/licensing.py`: uses Python stdlib `hmac` /
  `hashlib` (not cryptography); the filing's HMAC-SHA256
  reference was actually about stdlib. Even less risk than
  expected.

cryptography 48.0 removed some legacy hashes per upstream
release notes; Bibliogon uses none of them.

Tests:
- Focused (licensing + credential_store + ssh_keys): 71 / 71
  green.
- Full backend: 1626 / 1626 green.
- Launcher: 196 / 196 green.
- Launcher PyInstaller `--clean --noconfirm`: builds.
- `make sync-versions-check` + `make verify-plugin-locks`:
  both clean.

Deferred (not filed; not Bibliogon-runtime impact): the 4 pip
CVEs that pip-audit reported in both backend + launcher venvs
(`pip 25.2` / `26.0.1` with CVE-2025-8869, CVE-2026-1703,
CVE-2026-3219, CVE-2026-6357). pip is a Poetry-tooling dep,
not a Bibliogon runtime dep — the production Docker image
ships its own pip via `python:3.12-slim` and the launcher
binary doesn't bundle pip. These CVEs only affect a developer
machine running Poetry against malicious packages. Out of
scope for this fix.

## Archived 2026-05-13 (BACKEND-UPLOAD-SIZE-LIMIT-01)

### BACKEND-UPLOAD-SIZE-LIMIT-01 — body-size cap for every POST/PUT/PATCH

Filed 2026-05-12 by the v0.31.0 dep-audit chain as defense-in-
depth. No specific user report; closed proactively on
2026-05-13 after the BACKUP-HISTORY-SINGLETON-01 close because
the surface fits the same "small, high-value-per-effort, no
external dependency" profile.

Before this fix, only the cover-upload endpoint had a per-
endpoint size guard (~10 MB via the existing
`PayloadTooLargeError`). Every other upload endpoint — Medium
import ZIPs (the frontend caps at 200 MB but the backend was
unbounded), backup .bgb imports, plugin ZIP install, asset
uploads, AI-template ZIP import — would accept arbitrary-size
bodies, exposing a memory-DoS vector.

What landed (1 commit, `5c41d46`):

- `backend/app/middleware/body_size_limit.py`: new ASGI
  `BodySizeLimitMiddleware`. Two enforcement points:
  1. **Content-Length pre-check**: every well-behaved client
     (fetch / XHR / curl POST) sets Content-Length;
     oversized requests return HTTP 413 before any body byte
     is consumed.
  2. **Streamed body counter**: chunked-transfer clients
     (no Content-Length) get a wrapped `receive` that
     accumulates byte counts and aborts with 413 the moment
     the cap is exceeded; wrapped `send` prevents the inner
     handler from leaking a partial response.
  Method allowlist: GET / HEAD / OPTIONS / DELETE bypass
  entirely. Fail-open posture: config-load errors log at
  WARNING but the middleware falls back to the default cap.
- `backend/app/main.py`: middleware registered alongside
  CORSMiddleware; config read once at startup via the
  existing `_load_app_config()` helper.
- `backend/config/app.yaml` + `.example`: new
  `app.max_upload_mb` key (default 500). Editing requires
  a server restart — a runtime cap change would need
  locking around the in-flight request set.
- Per-endpoint caps stay (e.g. cover upload's ~10 MB);
  this is the outer fence, not a replacement.

Tests (+15 in `test_body_size_limit.py`):
- Resolver: 7 tests covering integer / string-int / missing
  / non-positive / non-integer / None paths.
- Integration via TestClient with a 1 KB cap on a single-
  endpoint app: 8 tests covering under-cap pass, at-cap
  pass, over-cap 413, GET/DELETE bypass, JSON-body shape
  for the ApiError contract.
- Full backend suite: 1611 → 1626 (+15, +2 from
  BACKUP-HISTORY-SINGLETON-01 earlier in the session).

Deferred: per-endpoint guards for medium-import and
backup-import. The outer 500 MB middleware covers the DoS
vector; tightening individual endpoints (e.g. backup-import
could refuse > 100 MB outright) is a follow-up if a real
user-flow needs the tighter ceiling. Not filed; reach for
on first user-report basis.

---

## Archived 2026-05-13 (BACKUP-HISTORY-SINGLETON-01)

### BACKUP-HISTORY-SINGLETON-01 — converge multi-instance backup history through disk

Filed 2026-05-13 alongside the v0.31.0 Phase 2 path-isolation
work. The trigger was active at filing time (the Playwright
smoke spec `import-flows.spec.ts::backup export adds a history
entry` was red); closed on the same day as the next-most-
important backlog item after v0.31.0 shipped.

Root cause: three modules each instantiate their own
`BackupHistory()` at module import time:
- `backend/app/routers/backup.py:24`
- `backend/app/services/backup/backup_export.py:22`
- `backend/app/services/backup/backup_import.py:26`

Before the fix, instance B's `_entries` was set at `__init__`
and never refreshed. The GET `/api/backup/history` endpoint
(served from `routers/backup.py`'s instance) never saw writes
that the export service made through its own instance. A
second, related, multi-worker bug also existed: without
`_load()` in `add()`, a second worker's stale `_entries` list
would clobber the first worker's writes on the next save.

What landed (1 commit, `c90d47d`):

- `backup_history.py`: `list()` and `add()` both call `_load()`
  first. The JSON file is the single source of truth; all
  instances + all uvicorn workers converge through it. Cost:
  one read per call; the file caps at 100 entries (~4 KB
  worst case).
- Module docstring rewritten to document the cross-instance
  consistency contract.
- 2 new regression tests in `test_backup_history.py`:
  - `test_list_sees_writes_from_other_instance_on_same_path` —
    reader-before-writer scenario mirroring the production shape.
  - `test_add_picks_up_writes_from_other_instance` — multi-
    worker write-clobber scenario.

Tests:
- 11 → 13 in `test_backup_history.py` (+2 regression pins)
- Playwright smoke `import-flows.spec.ts`: 7/7 green after the
  Docker dev backend restart that picked up the fix.

Deferred (not filed; reach for if symptoms surface): file-level
OS locks. Not needed for current load (small file, low write
rate); the Python GIL + the uvicorn worker model serialize
operations within a process, and the disk-write race window
across workers is narrow enough that the next reader's
`_load()` will pick up whichever write landed last. No
known production scenario hits this.

---

## Archived 2026-05-12 (LIST-VIEW-COMMENTS-COUNT-PARITY-01)

### LIST-VIEW-COMMENTS-COUNT-PARITY-01 — comments badge in the article list view

Surfaced during the 2026-05-12 list-view badge-overlap
diagnosis (stop condition fired: "comments-count badge
was added but never made it into the list view"). Filed
as P5 on the same day; triggered later that day on
parity + forward-compat grounds.

What landed (2 commits):

1. `04e84f1` — `refactor(frontend): extract CommentsCountBadge
   to shared component`. The badge previously inline in
   ``ArticleCard.tsx`` (commit ``87ab959``) was lifted into
   ``frontend/src/components/articles/CommentsCountBadge.tsx``
   so both card + list views share visibility logic,
   tooltip i18n, and icon treatment. Pure refactor; 7
   existing ArticleCard tests stayed green.

2. `25a153e` — `feat(frontend): comments-count badge in
   article list view`. Implementation option 2 from the
   pre-implementation analysis: integrate the badge into
   the ``.titleCell`` 1fr column instead of adding a 10th
   fixed grid column. Avoids any change to
   ``grid-template-columns`` (zero risk of re-triggering
   the just-fixed overlap regression at ``35222fc``) and
   avoids crushing the title column at tablet width.

Column-budget constraint documented in-commit: the 9-col
template sums to 720px fixed; adding a 50px 10th col
would have pushed the minimum to 770px, exceeding the
~768px tablet breakpoint.

Tests (+2 frontend; ArticleList.test.tsx now at 11):

  ``comments_count > 0``; zero-count row doesn't render
  the badge.
- Badge hidden when ``comments_count`` is undefined
  (legacy API responses pre-``fa0427d``).

Counts:
- Frontend: 927 → 929 (+2)
- Backend: unchanged

## Archived 2026-05-12 (MEDIUM-COMMENTS-UI-01)

### MEDIUM-COMMENTS-UI-01 — frontend surfaces for imported comments

Follow-up to MEDIUM-COMMENTS-IMPORT-01 (backend, archived same
day). Ships the three UI surfaces that make imported comments
visible to users: editor-sidebar comments panel, dashboard
count badge, Settings admin tab with list + filter + delete.

What landed (8 commits):

1. `fa0427d` — `feat(api): ArticleOut.comments_count computed field`
2. `3d109f8` — `feat(api): frontend client + types for comments`
3. (commit 3) — `feat(frontend): ArticleCommentsPanel in editor sidebar`
4. `87ab959` — `feat(frontend): comments-count badge on ArticleCard`
5. (commit 5) — `feat(frontend): Settings comments-admin tab`
6. `3f5fa83` — `feat(frontend): comment deletion in admin tab`
7. `fb09c05` — `feat(i18n): ui.comments.* keys across 8 catalogs`
8. (this) — `chore(close): MEDIUM-COMMENTS-UI-01`

Surfaces:

- **Editor sidebar (read-only)**: `ArticleCommentsPanel` renders
  comments below the AITemplatePanel. Plain-text body with
  `white-space: pre-wrap`; no TipTap dependency (every imported
  comment is structureless by the heuristic's definition).
  Loading is invisible (no spinner); empty state explicit;
  error banner surfaces ApiError.detail.
- **Dashboard count badge**: `ArticleCard` footer renders a
  Lucide MessageSquare + count when
  `Article.comments_count > 0`. Hidden when 0 or undefined
  (legacy responses).
- **Settings comments-admin tab**: new "comments" tab between
  Plugins and Support. Source-filter dropdown + orphans-only
  checkbox + Author / Body / Source / Status / Imported /
  Actions table. "Load more" pagination caps at 500 (server
  ceiling). Per-row Trash2 icon opens the simple useDialog
  confirm with an 80-char body preview substituted into the
  message. Optimistic row removal on success; row stays on
  failure for retry.

Backend changes (minimal, no new endpoints):

- `Article.comments_count` computed property (`len()` on the
  relationship filtered by `deleted_at IS NULL`).
- `ArticleOut.comments_count: int = 0` exposes it. Same
  precedent as `original_published_at`.
- `COMMENTS-COUNT-PERF-01` (P5) filed for the JOIN-counted
  subquery rewrite if per-article counts ever push above ~50
  routinely.

Architectural notes:

- **No editor-side deletion**: editor view is purely
  read-only in v1. Deletion only via Settings admin tab.
  Keeps the editor focused on writing.
- **No TipTap for body rendering**: plain text is enough
  for v1 since structureless content is the heuristic's
  definition. Future rich-renderer (commit deferred) can
  consume the persisted `body_json` if user demand emerges.
- **Single-item delete uses simple confirm**, not the
  bulk-delete type-to-confirm pattern. Low-stakes vs.
  potential mass-damage; the lighter UX is enough.
- **Native i18n** for de + en; English literals carried into
  the six auto-translated locales (el / es / fr / ja / pt /
  tr), matching the established pattern for app-side text
  pre-native-translator-review.

Counts:
- Backend tests: 1601 → 1604 (+3 from commit 1)
- Frontend tests: ~889 → ~926 (+37 across commits 2-6:
  +7 API client, +8 panel, +4 card badge, +10 admin section,
  +7 delete flow, +1 confirm-dialog passthrough sanity)
- i18n: 35 new keys across 8 catalogs, parity green

Testing lesson re-validated: React 18's StrictMode +
non-stable mocked `t` function strands the fetch effect on
every render. The admin-section delete test exposed it; the
fix was the `useRef(t)` pattern from the lessons-learned
rule "React useEffect deps + i18n test mocks: the t function
isn't stable."

Follow-ups still parked:

- `MEDIUM-COMMENTS-UI-V2-01` (would be P5 if filed): rich
  TipTap rendering for comment bodies, bulk-delete + re-link
  in the admin tab. Not filed yet - shipping if user demand
  emerges.

---

## Archived 2026-05-12 (MEDIUM-COMMENTS-IMPORT-01)

### MEDIUM-COMMENTS-IMPORT-01 — comment detection + storage for Medium imports

User reported a real-world artefact: among 209 imported
articles in the production export, at least one ("Thanks for
pointing that out — you're right, the link was missing.") is
a comment, not a top-level Article. Spec proposed a separate
`article_comments` table with heuristic-based routing, no
retro-fix for the existing 209.

What landed (10 commits):

1. `76d7cf0` — `feat(db): article_comments table + ArticleComment model`
2. `8d52015` — `feat(medium-import): comment-detection heuristic in walker`
3+4. `f0df93b` — `feat(medium-import): import_comments_mode + orphan_comment_handling settings`
5. `f37581a` — `feat(medium-import): route detected comments by mode`
6. `9358805` — `feat(api): GET /api/articles/{id}/comments`
7. `aa36c8c` — `feat(api): /api/comments admin router`
8. `579f1c0` — `test(medium-import): end-to-end coverage for all 3 modes + orphan handling`
9. `740f448` — `docs(help): comments-vs-articles section for medium import`
10. (close-out commit) — archive + backlog + journal + lessons-learned + UI-01 follow-up

Audit-driven design refinement: the spec's three-criteria
heuristic (body < 500 AND empty subtitle AND no struct) would
have missed 2 / 8 real comments in the user's corpus, including
their own reference case. The audit traced the cause to Medium
auto-filling `data-field="subtitle"` from the second paragraph
of the reply body when the author wrote no explicit subtitle.
Refinement: drop the empty-subtitle criterion. Detection went
from 6/209 to 8/209 with zero new false positives. The
audit + refinement is captured as a new lessons-learned rule
"Real-world data audit BEFORE implementation prevents
spec-vs-reality drift."

Counts:
- Backend tests: 1568 → 1598 (+30; target was +15)
- Plugin tests: +15 across walker + plugin

Architectural choices:

- **`responds_to_article_id` FK uses `ON DELETE SET NULL`**:
  deleting an article doesn't destroy its comments; they
  survive as orphans. Mirrors the orphan-handling default.
  (Note added 2026-05-12: the v1 Medium importer leaves
  `responds_to_url` `NULL` because the Medium HTML export
  carries no parent link to extract. The field is reserved
  for future importers whose export formats DO include the
  parent-article URL.)
- **Both endpoints in core, not the plugin**:
  `/api/articles/{id}/comments` in articles.py;
  `/api/comments` admin in a new comments.py. Future
  importers (WordPress, Hashnode) write to the same table
  and must not go through a Medium-plugin-prefixed route.
- **`imported_from = String(50)` hardcoded to `"medium"` for
  v1**. Enum table is overengineering at one value.
- **Backend-only scope**: no editor section, no count badge,
  no UI strings in this session. Comments invisible to users
  until MEDIUM-COMMENTS-UI-01 ships.

Follow-up filed: `MEDIUM-COMMENTS-UI-01` (P2) — comments
section in the article editor, count badge on the article
list, admin view for orphan management.

---

## Archived 2026-05-12 (AI-FILL-CAP-CONFIG-01)

### AI-FILL-CAP-CONFIG-01 — configurable per-batch caps for bulk AI operations

User asked to promote the second P5 follow-up from
UNIVERSAL-AI-TEMPLATE-02 Session 2 to active work. Goal: let
power-users raise the 50-item caps without forking the
repository.

What landed (1 commit, backend-only):

- **Config**: new `ai.bulk` block in
  `backend/config/app.yaml` (and `.example`) carrying
  `max_ai_fill: 50` and `max_ai_template: 50` with an
  `# INTERNAL` comment explaining what each cap guards.
- **Helper**: new `_get_bulk_ai_caps()` in
  `backend/app/ai/routes.py`. Reads the merged config fresh
  per call (same pattern as `_get_rate_limit_seconds`); a
  YAML edit takes effect on the next request. Non-int / zero
  / negative / None values fall back to the documented
  defaults (`DEFAULT_MAX_BULK_AI_FILL = 50`,
  `DEFAULT_MAX_BULK_AI_TEMPLATE = 50`) via
  `_coerce_positive_int`, so a typo never silently shrinks
  the cap.
- **Routers**: the Pydantic
  `Field(max_length=MAX_BULK_AI_*)` constraint is gone (a
  class-time constant can't reflect runtime config).
  Replaced with handler-side `_enforce_bulk_ai_*_cap`
  helpers that raise HTTPException 422 with the active cap
  surfaced in the error detail (e.g. `cap is 5`, or
  `ZIP contains 6 templates; cap is 5`). Affected endpoints:
  `bulk-ai-fill/estimate`, `bulk-ai-fill/start` (both for
  articles and books), `bulk-ai-template/export` (both),
  and `bulk-ai-template/import` (inline ZIP-count check).
- **Tests**:
  - New `tests/test_bulk_ai_caps.py` (12 unit tests for the
    helper: defaults, custom values, coerce-from-string,
    invalid-value fallback)
  - +2 in `test_ai_template_bulk_fill.py` (runtime cap
    raised lets a 51-id batch through; runtime cap lowered
    rejects a 5-id batch)
  - +3 in `test_ai_template_bulk.py` (export lower / raise,
    import ZIP-count check)

Design decisions documented in the session journal:

- Caps live under `ai.bulk` (not a new top-level key) for
  coherence with `ai.rate_limit_seconds` and `ai.model`.
- No env-var override: caps aren't secrets; the
  `_ENV_SECRET_OVERRIDES` table stays scoped to `ai.api_key`.
- No Settings UI: the backlog explicitly framed this as
  "configurable as plugin settings rather than hardcoded
  constants" — YAML editing IS the configuration mechanism.
  A Settings tab is a separate task with its own
  field-class authoring + i18n × 8 burden.

Counts:
- Backend: 1550 → 1568 (+18)
- Frontend: 889 (unchanged; backend-only feature)

Both Session 1 + Session 2 P5 follow-ups now closed:
BULK-AI-FILL-LIVE-COST-01 (live cost projection, archived
earlier today) and AI-FILL-CAP-CONFIG-01 (this entry).

---

## Archived 2026-05-12 (BULK-AI-FILL-LIVE-COST-01)

### BULK-AI-FILL-LIVE-COST-01 — live cost projection in the bulk AI-fill dock

User asked to promote the P5 follow-up from
UNIVERSAL-AI-TEMPLATE-02 Session 2 to active work. Goal:
surface a live "on pace to cost ~$X" projection in the bulk
AI-fill dock + modal during a running job so the user can
cancel mid-batch if the live burn rate disagrees with the
pre-flight estimate.

Trade-off documented in the original P5 filing: real per-call
costs only land after each LLM response, so an
early-burn-rate readout is noisy on small batches. Decision:
ship the projection unconditionally but render the `~` prefix
and the "projected" word so the approximation is honest;
let the user form their own judgment about when 1-3 priced
samples is enough signal vs. noise. The 10+ items threshold
mentioned in the original filing was a strawman; gating the
UI on it would only hide useful early signal during the
phase the user is most likely to want to cancel.

What landed (1 commit, frontend-only, no backend changes):

- **Context (`BulkAiFillJobContext.tsx`)**: new `pricedCompletedCount`
  state, incremented only when `item_done` reports a non-null
  `cost_usd`. New derived `costPerItemUsd` (= `totalCostUsd /
  pricedCompletedCount`) and `projectedTotalCostUsd`
  (= `costPerItemUsd * total`). Both are null until the first
  priced response lands. `projectedTotalCostUsd` is
  additionally null outside the `running` phase, because
  terminal phases already surface the authoritative final
  `totalCostUsd` via the `Cost:` row and a stale projection
  there would be misleading.
- **Dock (`BulkAiFillDock.tsx`)**: minimized badge gains a
  small "~{cost} projected" caption between the progress bar
  and the current-title line, shown only when phase is
  `running` and the projection is non-null. Modal totals
  strip gains two new pills, "Per item: ~${avg}" and
  "Projected: ~${total}", under the same gate.
- **i18n (×8 locales)**: three new keys
  (`ui.bulk_ai_fill.dock.projected`,
  `ui.bulk_ai_fill.modal.per_item_label`,
  `ui.bulk_ai_fill.modal.projected_label`). Native German +
  English; other six carry the English literals consistent
  with how the existing dock + modal block was authored. i18n
  parity test stays green.
- **Tests**: +5 context tests (initial null state, average +
  projection math, null-cost items excluded from priced
  average, projection nulled on terminal phase, projection
  null when `total == 0` to avoid Infinity), +2 dock tests
  (caption + pills appear after first priced item_done,
  pills removed on terminal transition).

Counts:
- Frontend: 882 → 889 (+7)
- Backend: 1550 (unchanged; the new feature is frontend-only)

The Session 1 follow-up **AI-FILL-CAP-CONFIG-01** (P5) stays
filed; this task did not promote it.

---

## Archived 2026-05-11 (BULK-DELETE-01)

### BULK-DELETE-01 — bulk-delete on Articles + Books dashboards

User asked for the same filter-aware selection model that powers
bulk-export to drive bulk-delete with two destinations: soft path
(trash, Undoable) and permanent path (gated by typing the
numeric count).

What landed (9 commits in one session):

- `backend/app/routers/bulk_delete.py` — `POST /api/articles/bulk-delete`
  and `POST /api/books/bulk-delete`, mirrored shape. Pydantic
  `BulkDeleteRequest { ids, permanent }` and
  `BulkDeleteResponse { deleted_count, skipped_already_trashed, failed[] }`.
  Cap `MAX_BULK_DELETE = 200` matches the bulk-export precedent;
  request rejected with 422 above. Soft path filters
  `deleted_at IS NULL` and lands already-trashed rows in the
  skipped list (idempotent). Permanent path cascades via SQLAlchemy
  `all, delete-orphan` (verified for Article→Publication/Asset/
  ImportSource and Book→Chapter/Asset/ImportSource).
- `frontend/src/components/dialogs/TypeToConfirmDialog.tsx` — new
  standalone component with numeric-count gating. Reuses the
  global `dialog-*` classes for visual parity with AppDialog.
  Standalone (not an AppDialog extension) because the destructive
  gating is operation-specific.
- `frontend/src/utils/formatActiveFilters.ts` — pure utility that
  turns ArticleFilters / BookFilters into "Status=draft, Sprache=de"
  for the confirm dialog. Returns null on no active filter so the
  filter block is hidden cleanly.
- `notify.bulkAction(message, onUndo, label)` — toast variant
  with an inline Undo button. Mirrors `notify.saveError` shape;
  10 s autoClose. Used by the soft path only — hard delete gets
  plain `notify.success` because the data is gone.
- `ArticleBulkActionBar` + `BookBulkActionBar` gain a Radix
  DropdownMenu trigger (In Papierkorb / Endgültig löschen). The
  trigger is disabled at `count < 2`; count=1 falls through to the
  existing row-menu single-item delete (`useDialog().confirm("danger")`)
  per the pre-inspection Q1 resolution.
- `ArticleList` + `Dashboard` wire the handlers, render one
  `TypeToConfirmDialog` for the permanent path with
  `formatActiveArticleFilters` / `formatActiveBookFilters` as the
  filter description.
- `ui.bulk_delete.*` × 8 i18n catalogs (26 keys per language). EN,
  DE authored; ES, FR, EL idiomatic; PT, TR, JA machine-translated
  and recorded in AUTO_TRANSLATED.md.
- Bilingual help-page section on both Articles and Books
  bulk-export pages.

Test counts: 9 backend behavior tests for the endpoints (soft path,
mixed-trash skip, missing-id-in-failed, permanent + cascade, Books
mirror, empty + over-limit 422). 10 Vitest tests for
TypeToConfirmDialog (initial-disabled, mismatch error, exact-match
enables, click + Enter both fire, Enter-on-invalid swallowed,
cancel, filter clause, ARIA). 8 tests for formatActiveFilters
(null on no filter, single + multi formatting, status=all elision,
sort-only doesn't count). Full Vitest suite still 759 at the
landing of the last commit; backend tests for the new module
9/9 green.

Pattern note: this is the first feature where the action-bar +
selection-hook decoupling really paid off. Adding two optional
handler props to each bar — no restructuring of the selection
state, no fork of the bar — got bulk-delete to ship in the same
session as the rest. Lessons-learned entry codifies the rule for
future bulk operations.

## Archived 2026-05-11 (MEDIUM-IMPORT-CONTENT-TRUNCATION-01 + MEDIUM-IMPORT-LANGUAGE-DETECTION-01)

### MEDIUM-IMPORT-CONTENT-TRUNCATION-01 — walker section-inner truncation

User reported "einige" (a few) Medium articles imported with
truncated content; pointed at "Wie Deutschland seine Unternehmer
ausbeutet" as the canonical case. Systematic survey of the
209-post production import revealed the actual scope was 117
articles (56%) with content loss, including 9 imports with zero
text. Root cause: `walker._walk_body` called
`section.find("div", class_="section-inner")` which returned
only the FIRST inner div per `<section class="section--body">`.
Medium's standard header-image layout puts THREE inner divs
per section (title, image lane, main body); the walker's
title-skip then dropped the only inner it had picked up, and
the main body was never processed.

Fix in commit `ce9665e`: iterate `find_all` over all inner divs.
Verified against the production worst case: pre-fix 170/3567
words (5%); post-fix 3562/3567 (99.9%).

Retro-fix in commit `18c2031`: re-walk source HTML for affected
articles. Materiality gate skips articles where the new content
is less than 2x the existing AND adds fewer than 100 words.
Image URL preservation: matches recovered ImageRefs against
existing ArticleAsset rows so already-downloaded images keep
their local URLs. Applied to the production corpus: 73 articles
materially recovered; 136 already complete; idempotent re-run
shows zero changes.

### MEDIUM-IMPORT-LANGUAGE-DETECTION-01 — auto-detect language via langdetect

User reported "some German articles correctly detected as
German" — DB inspection revealed the walker did NO language
detection and the importer hardcoded "en". The 2 German rows in
the production import had `updated_at > created_at`: user had
manually corrected them in the editor.

Fix in commit `bdf5c14`: walker runs langdetect over the body
text, surfaces `ParsedPost.detected_language`. Importer reads it
with `default_language` fallback. Confidence floor at 0.85
(picked from the production corpus where confident German /
English / Greek detections all scored ~0.99). Body text only,
not title/subtitle. Empty or <50-char bodies return None.

Retro-fix in commit `3af8ecb`: applies langdetect to existing
rows where `language == "en"` (the historical default).
Manually-corrected rows are preserved. Applied to the
production corpus: 81 rows updated (80 German + 1 Greek), 2
manual corrections preserved, 126 confirmed English. Zero
low-confidence rejections.

Final language distribution after retro-fix: 126 en + 82 de + 1 el.

### Cross-cutting

- New backlog item `BIBLIOGON-DATA-FIX-FRAMEWORK-01` filed
  under P3. The four scripts under `scripts/` (imageFigure,
  featured-image, truncation, language) share a common shape
  and should be refactored into a generic framework when a 5th
  one-shot is needed.

- Lessons-learned entries added: "Walker iterating repeated
  containers: prefer find_all over find" + "User impression of
  scope is anchored on what they noticed, not what's broken"
  (commit `c033944`). The session's two main bugs were both
  reported with quantitative scope estimates that the
  systematic survey contradicted.

---

## Archived 2026-05-09 (MEDIUM-IMPORT-FRONTEND-UI-01)

### MEDIUM-IMPORT-FRONTEND-UI-01 — Medium-import frontend page

Built the user-facing UI for the bulk Medium importer that landed
the day before in MEDIUM-IMPORT-MVP-01. The MVP backend was
verified and reachable via `curl`, but the target audience
(self-publishing authors) needed a UX-friendly path that does not
involve a terminal.

What landed (12 commits in one session):

- New top-level page at `/articles/import/medium`
  ([MediumImportPage.tsx](../../frontend/src/pages/MediumImportPage.tsx))
  with state machine `idle -> uploading -> processing -> result`.
  Diverges deliberately from the existing modal-from-page
  import-wizard pattern; rationale recorded in
  `.claude/rules/lessons-learned.md` ("Bulk operations with long
  processing time and structured results warrant page-route UX").
- `api.mediumImport.importZip` XHR helper in
  [client.ts](../../frontend/src/api/client.ts), the codebase's
  first XMLHttpRequest call. fetch() does not expose
  upload-progress events, and Medium archives can be tens of MB.
  Pattern stays scoped to this one helper; no XHR sprawl.
- 4 components in
  [components/medium-import/](../../frontend/src/components/medium-import/):
  `MediumImportUploadZone` (drag-drop + file picker, 200MB hard
  reject + 50MB soft warning), `MediumImportProgress` (two-phase
  determinate-bar / indeterminate-spinner), `MediumImportResult`
  (three Radix Collapsible sections: errored expanded by default,
  imported + skipped collapsed by default, deep links to
  `/articles/{id}`), `MediumImportSettings` (4 fields backed by
  the existing generic `api.settings.updatePlugin` —
  download_images, image_download_timeout_seconds,
  skip_existing_canonical_urls, default_status).
- Settings -> Plugins -> Medium-Import gains a pointer card
  ([Settings.tsx#L1892](../../frontend/src/pages/Settings.tsx#L1892))
  with "Medium-Import öffnen" navigating to the dedicated page.
  Preserves discoverability through the standard plugin-settings
  flow without duplicating the edit surface.
- "Aus Medium importieren" button on
  [ArticleList.tsx](../../frontend/src/pages/ArticleList.tsx)
  next to the existing import-wizard button.
- 46 i18n keys under `ui.medium_import.*` added to all 8
  backend catalogs (DE + EN authored, ES + FR + EL idiomatic for
  self-validation, PT + TR + JA machine-translated and tracked in
  `backend/config/i18n/AUTO_TRANSLATED.md`). Parity test green
  (43 tests).
- 24 Vitest tests across 5 new files (1 for the XHR helper,
  4 for the components). Full Vitest suite: 736 passed.
- Bilingual help page at
  [docs/help/{en,de}/articles/medium-import.md](../../docs/help/en/articles/medium-import.md)
  + `_meta.yaml` entry + regenerated `mkdocs.yml` nav.

Follow-ups created (still open):

- **BACKEND-UPLOAD-SIZE-LIMIT-01** (P3): backend body-size cap.
  Frontend hard-rejects >200MB but backend has no ceiling.
- **ASYNC-IMPORT-PROGRESS-01** (P2): real server-side progress.
  Current synchronous endpoint forces an indeterminate spinner
  during the processing phase; a 200-post archive can sit there
  for several minutes.

Premise correction during the session: the original Q1 resolution
chose route-based UX based on "consistent with existing import
wizard pattern at /import" — but inspection showed there is no
`/import` route; `ImportWizardModal` is a modal opened from
Dashboard + ArticleList. The user reaffirmed C-route knowingly,
accepting the divergence. Recorded in lessons-learned.

## Archived 2026-05-08 (MEDIUM-IMPORT-MVP-01)

### MEDIUM-IMPORT-MVP-01 — bibliogon-plugin-medium-import v1

User dropped a real 209-post Medium HTML export into the project
on 2026-05-08; previous-session audit identified the Article +
Publication + ArticleImportSource architecture as a near-perfect
fit and recommended a plugin shape matching KDP / audiobook /
kinderbuch precedent. This MVP shipped that plugin in 8 commits
across one session.

What landed:

- `backend/app/models/__init__.py` + Alembic migration
  `d8e9f0a1b2c3`: new `ArticleImportSource` table mirroring
  `BookImportSource` plus three forward-looking fields
  (`import_metadata` JSON, `importer_version`,
  `conversion_warnings` JSON list). `article_id` UNIQUE so the
  uselist=False relationship is enforced at the DB layer.
- `plugins/bibliogon-plugin-medium-import/` (10th plugin):
  pyproject + plugin.yaml + plugin.py + 8-language i18n labels +
  config YAML + Makefile + README. Path-dep wired into
  `backend/pyproject.toml` and `medium-import` added to
  `backend/config/app.yaml.example` plugins.enabled.
- `bibliogon_medium_import/walker.py`: BeautifulSoup-based
  HTML → TipTap walker handling every `graf--*` and `markup--*`
  class observed in the 209-post audit. Critical detail: Medium
  duplicates the page H1 as the first `graf--title` H3 in body;
  the walker skips exactly that one occurrence. `graf--h3` →
  TipTap heading level=2 (Medium maps user-typed H2 to graf--h3
  in body).
- `bibliogon_medium_import/image_downloader.py`: per-image
  download via httpx to
  `{upload_dir}/articles/{article_id}/imported_image/{filename}`,
  one ArticleAsset row per image, returns
  `{cdn_url -> served_path}` rewrite map applied to the TipTap
  doc before persistence. Per-image failures emit warnings but
  never abort the batch. Default-on per the data-sovereignty
  design decision.
- `bibliogon_medium_import/importer.py` + `routes.py`: bulk-ZIP
  endpoint at POST `/api/medium-import/import`. Per-post
  transactions (one bad post never rolls back the others).
  Dedup on `Article.canonical_url` (application-layer, no
  unique constraint, keeps a future `--update` flag flexible).
  Tolerant of single-wrapper-directory archives.
- `backend/app/routers/article_assets.py`: `imported_image`
  added to `_ALLOWED_ASSET_TYPES` so the existing
  serve-by-filename endpoint delivers downloaded images at
  `/api/articles/{id}/assets/file/{name}`.
- `docs/help/{en,de}/import/medium.md` + `_meta.yaml` + mkdocs
  nav regen. German prose uses real umlauts (UTF-8) per the
  lessons-learned rule.

Test coverage: backend 1308 → 1334 (+26). Plugin: 40 tests
covering walker (25), plugin scaffold (5), image-downloader pure
functions (10). Backend: model (6), downloader+DB (4), bulk
endpoint (11), API round-trip (5). All green.

Three Pre-inspection findings during scaffolding:

1. The audit said "dedup on `Publication.url`" but `Publication`
   has no `url` column. The correct dedup key is
   `Article.canonical_url` (real column on the Article model).
   Confirmed before commit 1.
2. PluginForge's BasePlugin uses `init(app_config, plugin_config)`
   to populate `self.config`; the constructor takes no args.
   First test run failed with `TypeError: takes no arguments`;
   fixed by following the BasePlugin contract.
3. Plugin endpoint tests need `with TestClient(app) as c:` (per
   the lessons-learned audiobook entry); plugin routes only
   mount during the FastAPI lifespan. Module-scoped fixture
   adopted.

Schema discipline: `BookImportSource` was already there as a
parallel pattern; `ArticleImportSource` mirrors it instead of
inventing a tag-based provenance scheme. Tag-based provenance
would have leaked `source:medium` into SEO-relevant metadata
that ships back to publishing platforms when articles are
cross-posted. The schema-extras (`import_metadata`,
`importer_version`, `conversion_warnings`) were added under the
"add fields that genuinely improve provenance" latitude clause.

Out of scope (deferred to v2 — see backlog P2):

- Dry-run preview UI: user imports everything and archives
  unwanted via the standard dashboard trash flow
  (`MEDIUM-IMPORT-V2-01`).
- AI-driven tag inference: imported articles ship with empty
  tags; user adds them per article in the editor. Substack and
  WordPress importer variants will benefit from the same
  AI-tag pipeline (`MEDIUM-IMPORT-V2-02`).

Commits: 8 in one session. (1) feat(db) ArticleImportSource +
migration. (2) feat(plugin) scaffold. (3) feat(medium-import)
walker. (4) feat(medium-import) image downloader. (5)
feat(medium-import) bulk ZIP endpoint + dedup + provenance. (6)
test(medium-import) round-trip via existing API surface. (7)
docs(help) bilingual page. (8) chore(backlog) close MVP + add
V2 followups (this entry).

## Archived 2026-05-07 (PLUGIN-LOCKFILE-DRIFT-01)

### PLUGIN-LOCKFILE-DRIFT-01 — gate the two-installation-paths divergence

Closes the discipline gap surfaced earlier in the same day: the
v0.30.0 release CI red-on-main from plugin lockfile drift after
the pre-v0.30.0 fastapi 0.135 → 0.136 dep sweep. Same shape as
MKDOCS-DISCIPLINE-01 (verify-the-gate); separate item because
the affected installation paths differ.

The shape under discipline: `make test` installs plugins via the
backend's combined `poetry.lock` (path-deps), but CI runs
`poetry install --no-interaction --no-ansi` **per plugin** against
THAT plugin's own `poetry.lock`. When a shared external pin
(e.g. fastapi) bumps in every plugin's pyproject but only the
backend lock gets regenerated, `make test` stays green while CI
turns red. The hotfix `3232fad` re-locked all 10 plugin lockfiles
manually.

Four commits address the gap at three lifecycle layers (commit,
gate-time, post-incident verify):

1. **`1b43aec` feat(make): lock-all-plugins + verify-plugin-locks.**
   Two new Makefile targets (for-loop over `plugins/bibliogon-
   plugin-*/`, per pre-inspection Q1: uniform operation, no
   per-plugin variation that would justify the existing
   per-plugin shortcut convention).
   - `lock-all-plugins`: iterates every plugin and runs
     `poetry lock`. Use after any shared-dep pin bump.
   - `verify-plugin-locks`: runs `poetry install --dry-run
     --no-interaction --no-ansi` per plugin, greps for
     "changed significantly", exits 1 with remediation hint.
     NOT in pre-tag chain (per Q4) — manual diagnostic only,
     since the pre-commit hook + CI cover the right times.
2. **`8f6fcea` feat(pre-commit): plugin pyproject.toml must be
   staged with its poetry.lock.** New local hook
   `plugin-lock-paired-with-pyproject` scoped via
   `files: ^plugins/bibliogon-plugin-[^/]+/pyproject\.toml$`.
   `scripts/check_plugin_lock_paired.py` consults
   `git diff --cached --name-only` to enumerate the staged
   set, asserts each hook-supplied pyproject path's sibling
   `poetry.lock` is also staged. Pyprojects without paired
   staged lockfile fail with a remediation hint covering the
   v0.30.0 incident, the `make lock-all-plugins` workflow, and
   a pointer to the lessons-learned entry. Per Q2: only
   pyproject-staging triggers; lockfile-only commits (e.g.
   follow-up after `poetry lock`) are valid and do not fire.
3. **`e31c4fd` test(pre-commit): hook self-check.** 6 tests in
   `backend/tests/test_plugin_lock_drift_hook.py` exercising
   the hook against an isolated git work-tree per test
   (option 3a per Q3 — the cheap path; the heavy path stays as
   the existing CI plugin matrix). Each test stages files,
   runs the hook, asserts exit code + key strings in stderr.
   All 6 tests pass in 0.22s. Joins backend pytest, so the
   gate fires on every `make test` (local + CI).
4. **`<this commit>` chore(backlog): close PLUGIN-LOCKFILE-DRIFT-01.**

The three gates fire at three lifecycle layers:

- **Commit time:** the pre-commit hook (commit 2) catches a
  plugin pyproject staged without its lockfile the moment a
  contributor stages it.
- **PR / CI time:** the existing `poetry install --no-interaction`
  per-plugin matrix in CI (unchanged by this work) is the heavy
  drift detection that catches actual lockfile content drift.
- **Manual diagnostic:** `make verify-plugin-locks` for power
  users who want to verify before push without invoking the
  full `make test`.

Lessons-learned cross-link: the morning's "Two installation
paths diverge: `make test` vs per-plugin CI" entry already
captures the meta-rule. This commit adds a one-line
"now enforced via PLUGIN-LOCKFILE-DRIFT-01" pointer to that
entry so future readers find the enforcement path from the
diagnosis.

Same-day archive (per Q6 / continuous-archival convention):
this entry archives the work in the same commit that closes
the backlog item. The PLUGIN-LOCKFILE-DRIFT-01 entry was
filed in commit `141b0f6` ~30 minutes ago and is closed here.

**Verification chain:**
- `make verify-plugin-locks` on current state: OK (10 plugins
  in sync after the morning's hotfix).
- `make test`: backend 1302 → 1307 (+5; 6 new test functions,
  one of them shares an assertion path so net +5), 1 skipped,
  full suite green in 67.94s.
- Pre-commit framework recognizes the new hook and runs it
  cleanly when no plugin pyproject is staged.
- Hook simulation tests (commit 3) all green at 0.22s.

---

## Archived 2026-05-07 (post-v0.30.0 MKDOCS-DISCIPLINE-01 + CI hotfix)

### CI hotfix: plugin lockfile drift after fastapi 0.135 -> 0.136

User flagged CI + Coverage red on main from the v0.30.0 release commit
`be4b6f3`. Root cause: the pre-v0.30.0 dep sweep bumped
fastapi `^0.135.0 → ^0.136.0` in 11 pyproject.toml files but only ran
`poetry lock` in the backend directory. Each plugin has its own
`poetry.lock` and the CI plugin matrix runs `poetry install
--no-interaction` per plugin, which fails with "pyproject.toml
changed significantly since poetry.lock was last generated" the
moment the pyproject pin drifts from the locked resolution.

Hotfix: `3232fad fix(ci): regenerate plugin lockfiles after fastapi
0.135 -> 0.136 bump`. Re-ran `poetry lock` in each of 10 plugin
directories. Verified green on the next CI run.

The shape — `make test` green but CI red — is the same shape as the
v0.30.0 retro's "verify the gate before trusting it" finding. New
lessons-learned entry added: "Two installation paths diverge:
`make test` vs per-plugin CI". Tracked as `PLUGIN-LOCKFILE-DRIFT-01`
(P3) for a follow-up session: `make lock-all-plugins` target + a CI
gate that flags staged plugin pyproject without paired lockfile
update.

### MKDOCS-DISCIPLINE-01 — five discipline improvements

Closes the docs-toolchain gap surfaced in the pre-v0.30.0
retrospective: `mkdocs build --strict` did not actually fail on
orphan pages because "not included in the 'nav' configuration" is
INFO-level, which strict mode ignores. Two pages
(articles/bulk-export.md, install/docker-desktop.md) sat orphan in
the public docs site for two release cycles before the docs+i18n
drift audit caught them.

Six commits address the gap:

1. **`bd0f554` fix(docs): detect orphan pages in mkdocs build via
   grep.** `scripts/check_mkdocs_orphans.sh` runs `mkdocs build
   --strict`, captures output, greps for the exact string
   `not included in the "nav" configuration`, exits non-zero if
   any orphan is found outside the explicit ALLOWLIST (single
   entry today: `SCREENSHOTS-TODO.md`).
2. **`b65e9c6` feat(docs): generate mkdocs.yml nav from
   _meta.yaml via marker blocks.** `scripts/generate_mkdocs_nav.py`
   replaced the previous whole-file-rewrite implementation with
   marker-block replacement (preserves comments + structure
   outside the marker pairs). Two marker pairs:
   `AUTO-GENERATED-NAV-START/END` inside the `nav:` block (after
   the hand-managed `Home: de/index.md` line), and
   `AUTO-GENERATED-NAV-TRANSLATIONS-START/END` inside the i18n
   plugin's `nav_translations:` block. `--check` mode exits 1 on
   drift with a unified-diff to stderr. New make targets:
   `sync-mkdocs-nav`, `verify-mkdocs-nav`, `check-mkdocs-orphans`,
   `verify-docs-discipline` (aggregate).
3. **`3315137` chore(release): add mkdocs nav verify + orphan
   check to pre-tag chain.** `release-workflow.md` Step 5 (Tests)
   bash chain now includes `make verify-docs-discipline` between
   `pre-commit run --all-files` and the launcher pyinstaller
   smoke build. Final-checklist item also added.
4. **`7e62979` feat(docs): pre-commit hook ensures help pages are
   in _meta.yaml.** `scripts/check_help_meta_completeness.py` runs
   under `.pre-commit-config.yaml` `local` repo, scoped via
   `files: ^docs/help/(en|de)/.*\.md$`. Fails when a staged help
   page's slug is missing from `_meta.yaml` and prints a YAML
   snippet the contributor can paste. Allowlist:
   `index.md` (landing pages have a different contract per
   pre-inspection Q2).
5. **`9ea4ff6` test(docs): enforce bilingual parity for help
   pages.** `backend/tests/test_docs_parity.py` (3 tests) walks
   `docs/help/en/` and `docs/help/de/`, asserts the file sets
   match modulo `EXCEPTIONS_INDEX_BASENAMES = {"index.md"}`. Zero
   asymmetries on v0.30.0 state — test passes out of the gate.
   Joins the backend pytest suite, so the gate fires on every
   `make test` (local + CI), not only at release time.
6. **`<this commit>` chore(backlog): close MKDOCS-DISCIPLINE-01,
   add PLUGIN-LOCKFILE-DRIFT-01, lessons-learned entry.**

The five discipline improvements together address the gap at four
different layers of the lifecycle:

- **Commit time:** the pre-commit hook (commit 4) catches a new
  page added without an `_meta.yaml` entry the moment a
  contributor stages it.
- **Pull-request / CI time:** the bilingual parity test (commit
  5) runs on every push as part of the backend pytest suite.
- **Release time:** the pre-tag chain (commit 3) bundles
  `verify-mkdocs-nav` + `check-mkdocs-orphans` (commits 1+2) as
  a MANDATORY gate before tagging.
- **Documentation drift:** the SoT pattern (commit 2) eliminates
  the hand-maintained-twice failure mode by deriving mkdocs.yml
  from `_meta.yaml` deterministically.

The retro's commitment "verify the gate before trusting it" turns
into a concrete property: `mkdocs build --strict` exits 0 with
orphan pages, so we wrote our own gate (commit 1) that actually
fails the build. A future version of mkdocs-strict mode that
escalates orphan-INFO to WARNING would let us drop our wrapper —
but until then, the wrapper is the gate.

---

## Archived 2026-05-07 (v0.30.0 release)

### v0.30.0 release — launcher i18n complete + DEP-DBPATH cycle closes

Released v0.30.0 (commit `be4b6f3`, tag `v0.30.0`). 28 commits
since v0.29.0; 57 files changed (+3889/-787 LOC). Minor bump
per SemVer; the breaking-style `BIBLIOGON_DB_PATH` removal sits
under "Action required" in the release notes since it had a
two-release deprecation runway (v0.27.0 warning, v0.28.0
precedence flip, v0.30.0 removal).

**Launcher i18n complete.** Catalog grew from 2 to 8 languages
(en/de/el/es/fr/pt/tr/ja). OS-locale resolver expanded with
`_OS_LOCALE_PREFIXES` tuple covering all 8 languages. Six new
native-name labels in en + de catalogs (Ελληνικά, Español,
Français, 日本語, Português, Türkçe). Three user-validated
catalogs (el/fr/es); three with `_meta.review_status:
"pending native speaker"` markers (pt/tr/ja). 31 new parity
tests enforce key parity, non-empty values, placeholder parity,
and marker contracts both directions.

**DEP-DBPATH-01 cycle closes.** Step 3 removes
`BIBLIOGON_DB_PATH` as a path override. Priority chain
collapses to TEST → DATABASE_URL → BIBLIOGON_DATA_DIR →
platformdirs default. Warning-only fallback if the var is still
in env; the warning will be removed in a later release. The
deprecation cycle (v0.27.0 warning → v0.28.0 precedence flip →
v0.30.0 removal) is documented in `lessons-learned.md` as a
worked example of the "warning, then flip, then remove"
deprecation pattern.

**5 new bilingual core help pages.** `developers/architecture.md`,
`developers/contributing.md`, `developers/deployment.md`,
`developers/api-reference.md`, `books/bulk-export.md`,
`install/cross-platform-installers.md`. Existing
`developers/plugins.md` refreshed for Vite 8 + Node 24.

**Pre-release dep sweep.** Three commits per the "discrete
commit, not release blocker" pattern: backend + 10 plugins
(fastapi 0.135 → 0.136 lock-step, uvicorn 0.44 → 0.46,
python-multipart, ruamel-yaml + in-range patches), frontend
(8 in-range packages via npm update), launcher (pyinstaller
6.19 → 6.20 in-range). 7 majors deferred per the
major-bumps-get-their-own-session rule.

**Pre-v0.30.0 retrospective.** `docs/journal/retrospective-pre-v0.30.0.md`
covers the v0.27.0 → HEAD period in 6 sections (shipped /
worked / struggled / approach shifts / patterns to watch /
commitments). Five concrete commitments for v0.30.0+ each
with what / why / how-enforced / failure-mode-if-abandoned.

**Pre-tag verify chain green.** `make test` (backend 1299 +
1 skipped, frontend 712, plugins green), tsc clean, ruff +
mypy clean, pre-commit clean, smoke 191/191 (2 flakes
retried clean — keywords-editor and import-flows; v0.30.0
changes do not touch those code paths), launcher
pyinstaller smoke build clean.

**Backlog deltas.** Closed: DEP-DBPATH-01 (cycle complete),
"Launcher localization beyond EN/DE" (shipped as the 8-language
expansion). Added earlier in period: LAUNCHER-I18N-NATIVE-REVIEW-01
(P5; tracking pt/tr/ja native-speaker review). Open-task count
holds at 4 active P3..P5 + 2 BLOCKED-on-upstream + 1 P5.

**GitHub release published** at
https://github.com/astrapi69/bibliogon/releases/tag/v0.30.0
with the per-release notes file at
`changelog/releases/v0.30.0.md`.

## Archived 2026-05-07 (DEP-DBPATH-01 step 3)

### DEP-DBPATH-01 step 3 — BIBLIOGON_DB_PATH override removed

Closes the `BIBLIOGON_DB_PATH` deprecation cycle begun in v0.27.0.
Step 1 (deprecation warning, v0.27.0) and step 2 (precedence flip
making `BIBLIOGON_DATA_DIR` the senior source, v0.28.0) shipped in
prior releases. Step 3 — full removal of the override — lands
between the v0.29.0 tag and the next release tag, accumulated on
`main`.

**Behavior change.** `BIBLIOGON_DB_PATH` is no longer honoured for
path resolution. The resolver in `backend/app/database.py`
short-circuits the env var: if it is set in the environment, a
single warning is logged at startup naming the ignored value, and
path resolution proceeds through the normal `BIBLIOGON_DATA_DIR`
or platformdirs default chain. The warning will be removed in a
later release once existing deployments have migrated.

The new resolution priority is:

1. `BIBLIOGON_TEST=1` → `TEST_DATABASE_URL` or `:memory:`.
2. `DATABASE_URL` (verbatim).
3. `BIBLIOGON_DATA_DIR` derivation → `<DATA_DIR>/bibliogon.db`.
4. Platformdirs default via `app.paths.get_db_path()` (Linux/macOS
   `~/.local/share/bibliogon/`, Windows `%LOCALAPPDATA%\bibliogon\`,
   Docker `/app/data` via the container env-var).

**Tests.** `backend/tests/test_database_url_resolution.py`
rewritten to match the new behavior (6 tests, all green):

- `test_db_path_alone_is_ignored_with_warning` — DB_PATH alone:
  resolver falls through to platformdirs default; warning emitted.
- `test_db_path_with_data_dir_is_ignored_with_warning` — both
  set: DATA_DIR-derived path used; same warning emitted.
- `test_data_dir_alone_does_not_warn` — clean DATA_DIR path; no
  warning.
- `test_neither_env_var_set_does_not_warn` — bare default path;
  no warning.
- `test_database_url_takes_precedence_over_db_path` — DATABASE_URL
  short-circuits including the DB_PATH ignore-warning path.
- `test_test_mode_short_circuits_all_overrides` — BIBLIOGON_TEST
  forces `:memory:` regardless of the other vars.

**Docs.** README.md, README-de.md, and the bilingual deployment
guide (`docs/help/{en,de}/developers/deployment.md`) updated to
mark `BIBLIOGON_DB_PATH` as **Removed in v0.30.0** with the full
deprecation timeline (warning v0.27.0, precedence flip v0.28.0,
removal v0.30.0). The variable row stays in the env-var tables
for one release cycle so users with existing `BIBLIOGON_DB_PATH=`
in their environment can find an explicit "this no longer works"
entry rather than wondering why the doc forgot about it. A later
release drops the row entirely.

**No Docker / launcher / installer impact.** `docker-compose.prod.yml`
sets only `BIBLIOGON_DATA_DIR=/app/data`; no installer script
references DB_PATH. Existing default deployments are unaffected;
only deployments that historically set `BIBLIOGON_DB_PATH` need to
remove it from their environment (the warning at startup names
the value).

**Verification.** `make test` green (backend 1298 + 1 skipped),
ruff + mypy clean, DE content sweep clean (no umlaut
transliterations introduced in the new doc rows).

The next release tag will pick up step 3 along with the post-
v0.29.0 backlog items (docs+i18n session and EL/ES/FR i18n
corrections) and ship as v0.30.0.

---
